# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# HTTP Health Check Endpoint Conventions Across Go Projects

## Your Task

Find and compare how /healthz and /readyz endpoints are implemented across kubernetes/kubernetes, grafana/grafana, and prometheus/prometheus. Identify the Go source files in each repo that register these endpoints and what checks each performs (DB, cache, dependencies).

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

Perfect! I've completed the analysis and created the comprehensive answer file. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary of Health Check Endpoint Implementations

**Kubernetes (github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes)**
- Has a sophisticated health check framework with three endpoints: `/healthz`, `/livez`, and `/readyz`
- Uses a pluggable health check system with built-in checks for:
  - Ping (baseline health)
  - Logging system health
  - Informer synchronization
  - Graceful shutdown
  - Database (etcd) connectivity and readiness
- Supports grace periods for livez (startup tolerance) but strict requirements for readyz

**Prometheus (github.com/prometheus/prometheus)**
- Simple, lightweight approach with two endpoints: `/-/healthy` and `/-/ready`
- `/-/healthy` always returns 200 OK
- `/-/ready` uses state-based checking via internal atomic flag
- Supports Ready, NotReady, and Stopping states
- No complex health checks - just simple readiness state management

**Grafana (github.com/grafana/grafana)**
- Proxies the Kubernetes endpoints (`/healthz`, `/livez`, `/readyz`) to its embedded Kubernetes apiserver
- Reuses the battle-tested Kubernetes health check framework
- Inherits all Kubernetes health check capabilities including etcd checks

The analysis identifies 7 key source files, 22 relevant symbols, and a complete implementation chain showing how health checks flow from configuration through installation to HTTP handler registration.

HTTP Health Check Endpoint Implementations Across Kubernetes, Grafana, and Prometheus\\n\\n## Overview\\nThe three projects use different approaches to implement health check endpoints:\\n\\n## Kubernetes (github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes)\\nKubernetes uses a comprehensive health check framework with three distinct endpoints:\\n\\n### Endpoints\\n- **/healthz**: General health status\\n- system health, ensures logs are not blocked\\n   - **InformerSyncHealthz** (NewInformerSyncHealthz, line 105-109): Waits for cache synchronization of informers\\n   - **ShutdownHealthz** ready to serve requests\\n   - **Multi-server overrides** (lines 371-411): Supports multiple etcd server configurations with separate health checks for each override\\n\\n4. **Handler Installation** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/healthz.go, lines 124-140):\\n   - `installHealthz()` installs the /healthz endpoint\\n   - `installReadyz()` installs the /readyz endpoint with a callback for lifecycle signals\\n   - `installLivez()` installs the /livez endpoint\\n   - Each endpoint can have multiple health checks aggregated via `healthCheckRegistry`\\n\\n5. **Grace Periods and Delayed Checks** (healthz.go, lines 142-167):\\n   - Livez checks support grace periods during startup (via `delayedHealthCheck`)\\n   - Readyz has no grace period - must pass before server accepts traffic\\n uses a simpler, state-based approach:\\n\\n### Endpoints\\n- **/-/healthy**: HTTP health status\\n- **/-/ready**: HTTP readiness status\\n\\n### Implementation (web/web.go)\\n\\n1. **Simple Response Handlers** (lines 591-604):\\n   - `/-/healthy` (line 591-597): Always returns 200 OK with message \\\"{AppName} is Healthy\\\"\\n   - `/-/ready` (line 598-604): Wrapped by `readyf()` middleware that checks internal state\\n   - Both support GET and HEAD methods\\n\\n2. **State-Based Readiness** (lines 658-677):\\n   - `testReady()` function checks `h.ready` atomic value\\n   - Returns 200 OK if state is `Ready`\\n   - Returns 503 Service Unavailable if state is `NotReady` or `Stopping`\\n   - Sets `X-Prometheus-Stopping` header to indicate shutdown state\\n\\n3. **Ready States** (web/web.go):\\n   - `Ready`: Server is operational and ready for requests\\n   - `NotReady`: Server is initializing\\n   - `Stopping`: Server is shutting down\\n\\n4. **No Complex Health Checks**: Unlike Kubernetes, Prometheus doesn't perform detailed component checks. It relies on a simple atomic ready flag that must be set externally.\\n\\n## Grafana (github.com/grafana/grafana)\\nGrafana adopts Kubernetes' health check framework:\\n\\n### Endpoints\\n- **/livez**: Via proxy to Kubernetes apiserver\\n- **/readyz**: Via proxy to Kubernetes apiserver\\n- **/healthz**: Via proxy to Kubernetes apiserver\\n\\n### Implementation (pkg/services/apiserver/service.go, lines 211-214)\\nGrafana doesn't implement custom health checks but instead proxies the endpoints to its embedded Kubernetes apiserver:\\n\\n```\\ns.rr.Group(\\\"/livez\\\", proxyHandler)\\ns.rr.Group(\\\"/readyz\\\", proxyHandler)\\ns.rr.Group(\\\"/healthz\\\", proxyHandler)\\n```\\n\\nThe `proxyHandler` forwards requests to `s.GenericAPIServer`, which is a standard Kubernetes apiserver that inherits all its health check infrastructure.\\n\\n### Benefits of Grafana's Approach\\n- Reuses battle-tested Kubernetes health check framework\\n- Automatic support for etcd health checks\\n- Consistent with Kubernetes ecosystem expectations\\n- Supports informer sync checks for APIServer resources\\n\\n## Key Differences\\n\\n1. **Complexity**: Kubernetes > Grafana > Prometheus\\n2. **Dependency Checks**:\\n   - Kubernetes: Etcd connectivity, informer synchronization, logging\\n   - Prometheus: Simple atomic flag\\n   - Grafana: Inherits Kubernetes checks\\n3. **Graceful Shutdown**:\\n   - Kubernetes: Dedicated shutdown checks\\n   - Prometheus: Separate stopping state\\n   - Grafana: Uses Kubernetes mechanism\\n4. **Response Codes**:\\n   - All three return 200 for healthy/ready states\\n   - All return 5xx for not-ready states\\n5. **Endpoint Naming**:\\n   - Kubernetes/Grafana: /healthz, /livez, /readyz (REST style)\\n   - Prometheus: /-/healthy, /-/ready (special prefix style)\\n\"\n}\n",
